tiff2geotiff - segmentation fault

10 posts / 0 new
Log in or register to post comments
Last post
April 9, 2017 - 4:09pm
#1
milan.salek_661499
tiff2geotiff - segmentation fault
Hello, I have followed carefully the tutorial of using NCL images in VAPOR (https://www.vapor.ucar.edu/sites/default/files/docs/VAPOR-WRF-NCL.pdf) but have had difficulties with the conversion of tiffs to geotiffs (commanded inside the NCL script wrf_Height_Final.ncl). The NCL script can create the image "plt_HeightLevel_temp.tiff" but then the utility tiff2geotiff results always in "Segmentation fault". Tested in Lubuntu 16 under VirtualBox and standalone powerfull PC machine (XEON processor, 16 GB RAM) running CentOs 7, all with the same results. I have tested the version 2.5.0, 2.6.0RC1 and development version 3.0.0, always with the same error. Interestingly, when I prepare the "non-georeferenced" tiffs and run the program tiff2geotiff in Windows at a notebook }runnig VAPOR 2.6.0RC1), it runs OK and adds the georeference info to the "plain" tiffs. The Linux version is apparently broken at all of the Linux machines I could use. The command (prompted by the NCL script or written in bash separately) and the output are as follows: tiff2geotiff -4 " +proj=lcc +ellps=WGS84 +lon_0=10 +lat_0=50 +lat_1=45 +lat_2=55" -m ./plt_HeightLevel.dat ./plt_HeightLevel_temp.tiff ./plt_HeightLevel.tiff Segmentation fault (core dumped). I have checked almost everything,have even experimented with setting of PATH, LD_LIBRARY_PATH etc but without success. I have searched the Internet but have not found any hint how to solve the issue. Any ideas?

#2
samuelli
Hello Milan, Thanks for your bug report, and we're looking into it right now. Unfortunately, I couldn't reproduce the problem on my system. Would you help answer the following questions so I could have a better sense on what next steps to take? 1) What version of NCL are you using? 2) Did you download the NCL binary or build it by yourself? 3) Did you download VAPOR binaries or build it by yourself? Thanks, Samuel

(Reply to #2) #3
milan.salek_661499
Hello Samuelli, thank you for the reaction. I am using NCL 6.3.0, downloaded and installed as binary in /opt, all environmental variables are set correctly. I am using NCL very often and without problems. Regarding VAPOR, I have downloaded all the VAPOR versions as binaries (2.5.0, 2.6.0RC0, even experimental 3.0.0; when using the particular version, all settings are changed accordingly), my attempt to compile it myself failed. I am using the Vapor in Linux mostly for WRF data preparation, the vaporgui is being used almost exclusively in Windows 10. I have tried the tiff2geotiff program in Linux (Lubuntu 16 and CentOS 7) with several settings (and even users, some of them in English locales), LD_LIBRARY_PATH is unset, but all the attempt failed with the report "Segmentation fault". Fortunately, the tiff2geotiff.exe program works in Windows, which actually saves the VAPOR functionality for me. It could help me if I could compile the tiff2geotiff separately. I have downloaded the snapshot at https://sourceforge.net/p/vapor/git/ci/88d240c6586af5d02b144aa0f34297ac9... but have not been successful either because it is associated with the compilation of the whole VAPOR, which is apparently not trivial (for me). It puzzles me that I am probably the only one reporting the problem. Nevertheless, leaving aside this issue, VAPOR is really great.

#7
samuelli
Hi Milan, Would you like to try two more things to help us diagnose the problem? The first is to use an installer with debug on, so you can save a core dump file when it crashes, and we could analyze that core dump file. More specifically, you can download a custom installer at: https://drive.google.com/open?id=0B0dQMtxB89M0NzlVRmdaanRXQUk Install it, and run tiff2geotiff with gdb to save a core dump file. More details on how to save a core dump file could be found here: https://wiki.archlinux.org/index.php/Core_dump. The second thing to try is to save the intermediate files generated by the NCL script, and we examine if the intermediate files are correctly generated by NCL. To keep the intermediate files, you need to touch the "$VAPOR_HOME/share/examples/NCL/wrf2geotiff.ncl" file in the VAPOR installation, change the 4th line to be false: "_wrf2geotiff_DEBUG = False". Then rerun the script, and send us the intermediate files fed in tiff2geotiff. Let us know how they work! Thanks, Samuel
